It covers the Go wrappers that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Concepts](#core-concepts)\n2. [Map Creation](#map-creation)\n3. [Map Lifecycle](#map-lifecycle)\n4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n6. [Batch Operations](#batch-operations)\n7. [Event System](#event-system)\n8. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n9. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n10. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n11. [BPF Filesystem Paths](#bpf-filesystem-paths)\n12. [Configuration Methods](#configuration-methods)\n\n---\n\n## Core Concepts\n\n### The Map Type\n\nThe `Map` struct is the primary interface for interacting with eBPF maps. It wraps the underlying kernel map and provides synchronization, caching, and event tracking capabilities.\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    // Fields are not directly accessible; use methods instead\n}\n```\n\n### Key and Value Interfaces\n\nAll map operations require keys and values that implement specific interfaces.\n\n#### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\nKeys must be stringer-compatible and provide a factory method for creating new instances.\n\n#### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\nValues must also implement stringer and provide a factory method.\n\n#### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\nFor per-CPU maps, values must implement:\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs that implement MapValue\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\nThe `NewSlice()` method returns a slice that can hold values from all CPUs. This is essential for correctly reading per-CPU map entries.\n\n### Example Key and Value Types\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP [4]byte\n    Port uint16\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d.%d.%d.%d:%d\", k.IP[0], k.IP[1], k.IP[2], k.IP[3], k.Port)\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\ntype EndpointValue struct {\n    ID uint32\n    Flags uint16\n}\n\nfunc (v *EndpointValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"id=%d flags=%d\", v.ID, v.Flags)\n}\n\nfunc (v *EndpointValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &EndpointValue{}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Map Creation\n\n### NewMap: Basic Map Creation\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new Map instance with the specified configuration. The map is not yet created in the kernel; it must be opened or created separately.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The name of the map (base name, without path)\n- `mapType`: The kernel map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`, `ebpf.PerCPUArray`)\n- `mapKey`: A pointer to a sample key (used to determine key size)\n- `mapValue`: A pointer to a sample value (used to determine value size)\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: Flags to control map behavior (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Returns:** A pointer to a newly initialized Map (not yet created in kernel).\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nimport (\n    \"github.com/cilium/ebpf\"\n    \"golang.org/x/sys/unix\"\n)\n\ntestMap := NewMap(\"cilium_connections\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &EndpointKey{},\n    &EndpointValue{},\n    65536,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n### NewMapWithInnerSpec: Map with Inner Specification\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a map with an inner map specification, used for map-of-maps constructs.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- Same as `NewMap`, plus:\n- `innerSpec`: The specification for the inner map\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ninnerSpec := &ebpf.MapSpec{\n    Type:       ebpf.Hash,\n    KeySize:    4,\n    ValueSize:  4,\n    MaxEntries: 1024,\n}\n\nmapOfMaps := NewMapWithInnerSpec(\"cilium_map_of_maps\",\n    ebpf.HashOfMaps,\n    &EndpointKey{},\n    &EndpointValue{},\n    256,\n    0,\n    innerSpec,\n)\n```\n\n### OpenMap: Open Existing Pinned Map\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\nOpens an existing map that is already pinned to the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map on bpffs\n- `key`: Sample key type for this map\n- `value`: Sample value type for this map\n\n**Returns:** An opened Map instance, or an error if the map doesn't exist or cannot be opened.\n\n**Errors:** Returns an error if the path is not absolute or the map cannot be loaded.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nlogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\nexistingMap, err := OpenMap(\n    filepath.Join(CiliumPath(), \"cilium_endpoints\"),\n    &EndpointKey{},\n    &EndpointValue{},\n)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to open map: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer existingMap.Close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle\n\n### Open: Load Pinned Map into Memory\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens a pinned map from the BPF filesystem. If the map is already open, this is a no-op.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Idempotent: Multiple calls to `Open()` are safe\n- Acquires write lock internally\n- Returns immediately if already open\n\n**Returns:** An error if the map cannot be loaded from the specified path.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntestMap := NewMap(\"cilium_test\", ebpf.Hash, &TestKey{}, &TestValue{}, 1024, 0)\nif err := testMap.Open(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to open map: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer testMap.Close()\n```\n\n### OpenOrCreate: Open or Create Map\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map, or creates it if it doesn't exist. If the map exists but its attributes (type, key/value size, capacity, flags) don't match, the map is deleted and recreated without retaining its contents.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If map already exists and has matching attributes, it is opened and contents preserved\n- If map exists with mismatched attributes, it is deleted and recreated empty\n- If map doesn't exist, it is created and pinned to the BPF filesystem\n- Non-persistent maps are always recreated even if they exist\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nconnMap := NewMap(\"cilium_connections\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &ConnKey{},\n    &ConnValue{},\n    262144,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n).WithCache()\n\nif err := connMap.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to open or create map: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer connMap.Close()\n```\n\n### CreateUnpinned: Create Map Without Pinning\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates a map in the kernel without pinning it to the BPF filesystem. The map will be automatically cleaned up when the process terminates.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in memory only\n- Map is not persisted to bpffs\n- Useful for temporary maps or testing\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Returns:** An error if the map cannot be created.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntempMap := NewMap(\"cilium_temp\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &TestKey{},\n    &TestValue{},\n    1024,\n    0,\n)\nif err := tempMap.CreateUnpinned(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to create unpinned map: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer tempMap.Close()\n```\n\n### Create: Create and Immediately Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nConvenience method that calls `OpenOrCreate()` and then immediately closes the map. Useful for initialization where the map will be opened again later.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to: `OpenOrCreate()` followed by `Close()`\n- Leaves the map pinned to the filesystem\n- Useful in initialization routines\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_init_map\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1024, 0)\nif err := m.Create(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to create map: %v\", err)\n}\n// Map now exists on disk but is not open\n```\n\n### Recreate: Force Recreate Pinned Map\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves the pinned map from the filesystem and recreates it fresh, deleting all contents.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Unpin the map from bpffs\n- Delete the map file\n- Create and repin the map\n- All previous contents are lost\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Returns:** An error if the map is already open or if recreation fails.\n\n**Errors:** Returns an error if the map is currently open (`m != nil`).\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_stats\", ebpf.Hash, &StatsKey{}, &StatsValue{}, 10000, 0)\nif err := m.Recreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to recreate map: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### IsOpen: Check if Map is Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether the map is currently open.\n\n**Returns:** `true` if the map has been opened and is ready for operations.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif !m.IsOpen() {\n    if err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n        log.Fatalf(\"Failed to open map: %v\", err)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Close: Close Map\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map and releases its resources. The map remains pinned to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying kernel map file descriptor\n- Stops any error resolver controllers\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n- Safe to call multiple times\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Returns:** Any error encountered during cleanup.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup: Retrieve a Value\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves the value associated with a key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Returns a new MapValue instance (not a reference to internal data)\n- Acquires read lock internally\n- Safe to retain the returned value after the call\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to look up (must match the map's key type)\n\n**Returns:** The value associated with the key, or an error if not found or on failure.\n\n**Errors:**\n- `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`: Key is not in the map\n- Other errors from the kernel map operation\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nkey := &EndpointKey{IP: [4]byte{10, 0, 0, 1}, Port: 8080}\nvalue, err := m.Lookup(key)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        log.Println(\"Key not found\")\n    } else {\n        log.Fatalf(\"Lookup failed: %v\", err)\n    }\n} else {\n    log.Printf(\"Found value: %s\", value)\n}\n```\n\n### Update: Insert or Update a Value\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates a value in the map. If the key already exists, its value is replaced.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Creates new entry if key doesn't exist\n- Replaces value if key exists\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache\n- If events are enabled, records a MapUpdate event\n- If the operation fails and caching is enabled, schedules error resolution\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to insert or update\n- `value`: The value to store\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nkey := &EndpointKey{IP: [4]byte{10, 0, 0, 1}, Port: 8080}\nvalue := &EndpointValue{ID: 123, Flags: 0x01}\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Update failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Delete: Remove a Value\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry associated with a key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Returns error if the key doesn't exist\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache\n- If events are enabled, records a MapDelete event\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** An error if the key doesn't exist or the operation fails.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nkey := &EndpointKey{IP: [4]byte{10, 0, 0, 1}, Port: 8080}\nif err := m.Delete(key); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Delete failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### SilentDelete: Remove a Value (Ignore Missing Keys)\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes the entry associated with a key, but doesn't return an error if the key doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Same as `Delete()` but returns `(false, nil)` if the key doesn't exist\n- Returns `(true, nil)` on successful deletion\n- Useful for cleanup operations where missing keys are expected\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** `(true, nil)` if deleted, `(false, nil)` if key doesn't exist, or `(false, err)` on other errors.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nkey := &EndpointKey{IP: [4]byte{10, 0, 0, 1}, Port: 8080}\ndeleted, err := m.SilentDelete(key)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Delete failed: %v\", err)\n} else if deleted {\n    log.Println(\"Entry was deleted\")\n} else {\n    log.Println(\"Entry did not exist\")\n}\n```\n\n### DeleteLocked: Delete Within Callback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes an entry while the map lock is already held. This must only be called from within a `DumpCallback` to avoid deadlocks.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Assumes the map lock is already held for writing\n- Must be called only from within a callback passed to `DumpReliablyWithCallback()`\n- Calling from other contexts causes deadlock\n- Updates cache and events like `Delete()`\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n**Important:** This method requires special care to avoid deadlocks. Only call it from within a map dump callback.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // ... process entry ...\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Failed to delete: %v\", err)\n        }\n    }\n}, stats)\n```\n\n### DeleteAll: Remove All Entries\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and removing each entry individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates through all map entries\n- Deletes each entry individually\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache for each deletion\n- If events are enabled, records a MapDeleteAll event\n- Entries added during iteration may not be deleted\n- Updates pressure metrics if enabled\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif err := m.DeleteAll(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"DeleteAll failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### ClearAll: Reset All Entries to Zero\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nIterates through all map entries and resets them to zero values instead of deleting them.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Useful for per-CPU maps where we want to preserve the entries but reset values\n- Cannot be used with events buffer enabled\n- Cannot be used with value cache enabled\n- Iterates and updates each entry individually\n- Returns error if events buffer or value cache is enabled\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails or if incompatible configurations are active.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif err := m.ClearAll(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"ClearAll failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### DumpWithCallback: Basic Iteration\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in the map and calls a callback for each entry.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Calls the callback for each entry\n- Returns new MapKey and MapValue instances to the callback\n- Safe to retain values received in the callback\n- Acquires read lock internally\n- Cannot modify the map during iteration (would hang)\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function called for each entry\n\n**Returns:** An error if the iteration fails.\n\n**Errors:**\n- Empty callback returns error\n- Iteration errors from the kernel\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    ek := key.(*EndpointKey)\n    ev := value.(*EndpointValue)\n    log.Printf(\"Key: %s, Value: %s\", ek, ev)\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Dump failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### DumpPerCPUWithCallback: Per-CPU Iteration\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in a per-CPU map, retrieving values from all CPUs.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with per-CPU map types\n- Calls the callback with a slice of values (one per CPU)\n- Value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n- Safe to retain values received in the callback\n- Acquires read lock internally\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function called for each entry with values from all CPUs\n\n**Returns:** An error if the map is not a per-CPU map or the iteration fails.\n\n**Errors:**\n- Empty callback returns error\n- Error if map is not a per-CPU type\n- Error if value doesn't implement MapPerCPUValue\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype PerCPUStats []StatsValue\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) String() string { return \"stats\" }\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) New() MapValue { return &PerCPUStats{} }\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) NewSlice() any { return &PerCPUStats{} }\n\nerr := m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    cpuStats := values.(*PerCPUStats)\n    for i, stat := range *cpuStats {\n        log.Printf(\"CPU %d: %s\", i, stat)\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### DumpWithCallbackIfExists: Conditional Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback()`, but returns without error if the map doesn't exist on the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the map exists before dumping\n- Returns `nil` if the map doesn't exist\n- Otherwise behaves like `DumpWithCallback()`\n\n**Returns:** `nil` if the map doesn't exist, or the result of `DumpWithCallback()`.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallbackIfExists(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process entry\n})\n```\n\n### DumpReliablyWithCallback: Resilient Iteration\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    // Stats about the dump operation\n}\n\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over map entries with resilience to concurrent modifications. Tracks iteration state to handle entries deleted during iteration.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Handles entries deleted during iteration by backtracking\n- Caps the maximum number of iterations at 4 times the max map size\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if the limit is reached\n- Tracks current, previous, and next keys to handle deletions\n- Falls back to previously seen key if current key is deleted\n- Callback must not call map operations that acquire the map lock\n- Acquires write lock internally\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function for each entry\n- `stats`: Statistics object for tracking iteration state\n\n**Returns:** Error including `ErrMaxLookup` if iteration limit exceeded.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process entry\n}, stats)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ErrMaxLookup) {\n        log.Println(\"Iteration limit reached\")\n    } else {\n        log.Fatalf(\"Dump failed: %v\", err)\n    }\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Completed: %v, Lookups: %d\", stats.Completed, stats.Lookup)\n```\n\n### Dump: Get All Entries as Map\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nConvenience method that dumps all map entries into a Go map with string keys and slice of string values.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `DumpWithCallback()` internally\n- Converts keys and values to strings\n- Accumulates multiple values per key in a slice\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nresult := make(map[string][]string)\nif err := m.Dump(result); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Dump failed: %v\", err)\n}\nfor k, vals := range result {\n    for _, v := range vals {\n        log.Printf(\"%s -> %s\", k, v)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### DumpIfExists: Conditional Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump()`, but returns without error if the map doesn't exist.\n\n---\n\n## Batch Operations\n\n### BatchIterator: Typed Batch Iteration\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // Fields not directly accessible\n}\n\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nProvides type-safe batch iteration over map entries using the kernel's batch lookup API.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: The key type (e.g., `EndpointKey`)\n- `VT`: The value type (e.g., `EndpointValue`)\n- `KP`: Pointer type of key (automatically constrained to `*KT` where `*KT` implements `MapKey`)\n- `VP`: Pointer type of value (automatically constrained to `*VT` where `*VT` implements `MapValue`)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Uses the kernel's batch lookup API for efficient iteration\n- Automatically handles buffer sizing and retries on ENOSPC errors\n- Automatically doubles buffer size on ENOSPC and retries up to max retries\n- Type-safe: returns typed pointers to keys and values\n- Supports context cancellation\n- Can be reused; each call to `IterateAll()` resets internal state\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m)\nctx := context.Background()\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    log.Printf(\"Key: %s, Value: %s\", k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### IterateAll: Perform Batch Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns an iterator sequence for batch iteration over the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie map types\n- Automatically handles ENOSPC errors by growing buffer\n- Respects context cancellation\n- Resets error state on each call\n- Returns `iter.Seq2` for use with range loops\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for cancellation\n- `opts`: Optional iterator options (WithMaxRetries, WithStartingChunkSize, WithEBPFBatchOpts)\n\n**Returns:** An iterator sequence that yields key/value pointers.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 10*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\n\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    if err := processEntry(k, v); err != nil {\n        break\n    }\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Iterator Options\n\n#### WithMaxRetries\n\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nSets the maximum number of retries when encountering ENOSPC errors.\n\n**Default:** 3 retries\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m,\n    WithMaxRetries[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](5),\n)\n```\n\n#### WithStartingChunkSize\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nSets the initial chunk size for batch lookups.\n\n**Default:** Automatically calculated as `sqrt(max_entries * 2)` rounded up to nearest power of 2\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m,\n    WithStartingChunkSize[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](256),\n)\n```\n\n#### WithEBPFBatchOpts\n\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nProvides custom batch options to the underlying ebpf-go library.\n\n### Batch Iteration Retry Behavior\n\n**ENOSPC Error Handling:**\n- When a batch lookup fails with ENOSPC (buffer too small), the iterator automatically:\n  1. Doubles the buffer size\n  2. Retries the iteration at the same cursor position\n  3. Repeats up to `maxRetries` times (default 3)\n  4. Returns the error if max retries exceeded\n\nThis happens transparently in the iterator and doesn't restart iteration from the beginning.\n\n**Example Scenario:**\nFor an LRU hash map with uneven bucket sizes, a batch lookup might fail if one bucket is larger than the buffer. The iterator handles this by growing the buffer and retrying without losing progress.\n\n### CountAll: Count Map Entries\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nHelper function that counts all entries in a map using a batch iterator.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m)\ncount, err := CountAll(context.Background(), iter)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Count failed: %v\", err)\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Map contains %d entries\", count)\n```\n\n### BatchLookup: Low-Level Batch Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nLow-level batch lookup operation. Prefer `BatchIterator` for most use cases.\n\n**Returns:** The number of entries retrieved, or an error.\n\n### BatchCount: Count Entries\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts the number of entries in a map using batch lookup.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n- Handles ENOSPC errors by retrying with larger buffer\n- Efficiently counts without retrieving all data\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ncount, err := m.BatchCount()\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"BatchCount failed: %v\", err)\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Map has %d entries\", count)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\n### Event Types\n\nEvents are recorded for map operations when events buffer is enabled. Three action types are supported:\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota // m.Update() or m.resolveErrors() Insert\n    MapDelete                 // m.Delete() or m.resolveErrors() Delete\n    MapDeleteAll              // m.DeleteAll()\n)\n```\n\n### Event Structure\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // Action is available via GetAction()\n    // Key/Value available via GetKey()/GetValue()\n    // Error available via GetLastError()\n}\n\n// Methods:\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction\n```\n\n### DumpAndSubscribe: Event Streaming\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)\n```\n\nDumps existing events from the buffer and optionally subscribes to new events.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for the subscription (used when follow=true)\n- `callback`: Function called for each event\n- `follow`: If true, continue receiving new events; if false, only dump existing events\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If callback is nil, no existing events are dumped\n- If follow is true, callback continues to be called for new events\n- Prevents missed events between dump and subscription start\n- Acquires read lock internally\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\neventCount := 0\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    eventCount++\n    log.Printf(\"[%s] %s -> %s (err=%v)\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue(), e.GetLastError())\n}, true) // Follow new events\n\n// ... do some operations ...\n\n// Events are streamed to callback until context is cancelled\n```\n\n### IsEventsEnabled: Check Event Status\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether the events buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Understanding Pinning\n\nPinned maps are persisted in the BPF filesystem (bpffs). They survive program restarts but are lost if bpffs is unmounted.\n\n**Behavior Semantics:**\n- **Pinned maps** (created with `OpenOrCreate()` or `OpenMap()`): Persisted to bpffs, survive program restart\n- **Unpinned maps** (created with `CreateUnpinned()`): Stored in kernel memory only, released on program exit\n- **Map Recreation**: When opening an existing map, if attributes don't match, the pinned map is deleted and recreated (losing all data)\n\n### Unpin: Remove Pinned Map\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map from the BPF filesystem. The map remains open if already open.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the pinned map file from bpffs\n- The map continues to exist in kernel memory if currently open\n- Safe to call on non-pinned maps (returns error)\n\n**Returns:** An error if the file cannot be removed.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif err := m.Unpin(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Unpin failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### UnpinIfExists: Conditional Unpin\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map from bpffs only if it exists, returning no error if it doesn't.\n\n**Returns:** An error if the unpin fails (other than the map not existing).\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif err := m.UnpinIfExists(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"UnpinIfExists failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Map Persistence Behavior\n\n```go\n// Scenario 1: New map\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_new\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1024, 0)\nm.OpenOrCreate()  // Created and pinned\nm.Close()         // Still pinned, survives restart\n\n// Scenario 2: Reopen existing map with same attributes\nm2 := NewMap(\"cilium_new\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1024, 0)\nm2.OpenOrCreate()  // Opens existing map, contents preserved\nm2.Close()\n\n// Scenario 3: Reopen with different attributes\nm3 := NewMap(\"cilium_new\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 2048, 0)  // Different size!\nm3.OpenOrCreate()  // Detects incompatibility, deletes old map, creates new one\n// Previous contents are LOST\n\n// Scenario 4: Unpin and recreate\nm.Unpin()         // Remove from bpffs\nm.Recreate()      // Delete and recreate the map\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### Implementing MapKey\n\n```go\ntype ConnectionKey struct {\n    Local  uint32\n    Remote uint32\n    Port   uint16\n}\n\nfunc (k *ConnectionKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d:%d:%d\", k.Local, k.Remote, k.Port)\n}\n\nfunc (k *ConnectionKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &ConnectionKey{}\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must be a struct with fixed-size fields (will be binary marshalled)\n- String() must return a human-readable representation\n- New() must return a zero-initialized instance\n- Pointer receiver on all methods\n\n### Implementing MapValue\n\n```go\ntype ConnectionValue struct {\n    Established uint32\n    Packets     uint64\n    Bytes       uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *ConnectionValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"est=%d pkts=%d bytes=%d\", v.Established, v.Packets, v.Bytes)\n}\n\nfunc (v *ConnectionValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &ConnectionValue{}\n}\n```\n\n### Implementing MapPerCPUValue\n\n```go\ntype StatsPerCPU []StatsValue\n\ntype StatsValue struct {\n    Packets uint64\n    Bytes   uint64\n}\n\nfunc (s *StatsPerCPU) String() string {\n    total := uint64(0)\n    for _, stat := range *s {\n        total += stat.Packets\n    }\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"total_packets=%d\", total)\n}\n\nfunc (s *StatsPerCPU) New() MapValue {\n    return &StatsPerCPU{}\n}\n\nfunc (s *StatsPerCPU) NewSlice() any {\n    // Return a slice that can hold one value per CPU\n    return &StatsPerCPU{}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nCollection loading allows loading entire eBPF programs (with all maps and programs) from an ELF object file.\n\n### LoadCollection: Load Complete Program\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n    Constants      any\n    MapRenames     []map[string]string\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n    Keep           *set.Set[string]\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection (programs and maps) into the kernel.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `spec`: Collection specification from parsed ELF object\n- `opts`: Loading options\n\n**Returns:**\n- `*ebpf.Collection`: The loaded collection\n- `func() error`: Commit function (must be called after attaching programs)\n- `error`: Any error during loading\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Loads all programs and maps\n- Maps marked as pinned are loaded from bpffs if they exist and are compatible\n- Incompatible maps are recreated\n- Tail calls are resolved\n- Returns a commit function that must be called after programs are attached\n\n**Important:** The commit function must be called after all program attachments to complete map pinning for replaced maps.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nimport \"github.com/cilium/ebpf\"\n\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"path/to/program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"LoadCollectionSpec failed: %v\", err)\n}\n\nopts := &CollectionOptions{\n    CollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n        Maps: ebpf.MapOptions{\n            PinPath: CiliumPath(),\n        },\n    },\n}\n\ncoll, commit, err := LoadCollection(logger, spec, opts)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"LoadCollection failed: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer coll.Close()\n\n// Attach programs to hooks...\n// hostProgram.Attach(...)\n// netdevProgram.Attach(...)\n\n// Commit map pins after all programs are attached\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Commit failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### LoadAndAssign: Load and Assign to Struct\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nConvenience function that loads a collection and automatically assigns its programs and maps to struct fields.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `to`: Pointer to a struct to assign programs and maps to\n- `spec`: Collection specification\n- `opts`: Loading options\n\n**Returns:**\n- Commit function (same as LoadCollection)\n- Error if loading or assignment fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes struct fields to determine which objects to keep\n- Loads the collection with automatic field assignment\n- Returns commit function for later invocation\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype DatapathPrograms struct {\n    ToNetdev  *ebpf.Program  `ebpf:\"cil_to_netdev\"`\n    FromHost  *ebpf.Program  `ebpf:\"cil_from_host\"`\n    ConnTrack *Map           `ebpf:\"cilium_ct_tcp4\"`\n}\n\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"path/to/program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"LoadCollectionSpec failed: %v\", err)\n}\n\nvar progs DatapathPrograms\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, &progs, spec, opts)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"LoadAndAssign failed: %v\", err)\n}\n\n// Now progs.ToNetdev, progs.FromHost, etc. are populated\n// Attach programs and then commit...\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Commit failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### CollectionOptions Details\n\n**Constants:** Pointer to a struct with runtime configuration values that override compile-time defaults in the program.\n\n**MapRenames:** List of maps to rename during loading. This creates unique pin paths for maps that should have per-endpoint or per-version instances.\n\n**MapReplacements:** Maps the collection should reuse instead of creating new ones.\n\n**Keep:** Set of object names to keep during reachability analysis. Prevents unused code elimination.\n\n**ConfigDumpPath:** Path to write configuration values used during loading (for debugging/sysdumps).\n\n---\n\n## BPF Filesystem Paths\n\nThe BPF filesystem (bpffs) is where Cilium pins maps and programs for persistence and privileged access.\n\n### BPFFSRoot: Get BPF Filesystem Root\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n```\n\nReturns the root path where the BPF filesystem is mounted.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns the configured bpffs mount point\n- Typically `/sys/fs/bpf` on Linux\n- Can be customized before first call (via `setBPFFSRoot()`)\n\n**Returns:** Absolute path to the bpffs root.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nroot := BPFFSRoot()  // e.g., \"/sys/fs/bpf\"\n```\n\n### CiliumPath: Get Cilium-Specific Path\n\n```go\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path where Cilium stores its pinned objects within bpffs.\n\n**Returns:** Path like `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium`\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nciliumDir := CiliumPath()  // e.g., \"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium\"\n```\n\n### MapPath: Get Path for a Specific Map\n\n```go\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n```\n\nReturns the full path where a map with the given name would be pinned.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger (used for fallback mount info reading)\n- `name`: Map name\n\n**Returns:** Absolute path like `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/cilium_endpoints`\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\npath := MapPath(logger, \"cilium_endpoints\")\n// Returns: \"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/cilium_endpoints\"\n```\n\n### LocalMapName: Create Local Map Name\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nCreates a unique map name for a per-endpoint or per-resource instance.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: Base name for the map\n- `id`: Identifier (e.g., endpoint ID)\n\n**Returns:** Formatted name like `name00123` for id=123\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nmapName := LocalMapName(\"cilium_local_policy\", 1234)\n// Returns: \"cilium_local_policy01234\"\n```\n\n### LocalMapPath: Get Path for Local Map\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nReturns the full path for a locally-scoped map.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\npath := LocalMapPath(logger, \"cilium_local_policy\", 1234)\n// Returns: \"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/cilium_local_policy01234\"\n```\n\n### TCGlobalsPath: Get TC Globals Path\n\n```go\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path for legacy TC map pins.\n\n### CheckOrMountFS: Ensure BPF Filesystem is Mounted\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\nEnsures the BPF filesystem is mounted at the specified location (or default if empty).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if bpffs is already mounted at the specified path\n- Mounts it if necessary\n- Tries alternative locations if default is already used by another filesystem\n- Panics on fatal errors\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for error messages\n- `bpfRoot`: Desired root path, or empty for default (`/sys/fs/bpf`)\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\n// Use default location\nCheckOrMountFS(logger, \"\")\n\n// Or use custom location\nCheckOrMountFS(logger, \"/custom/bpf/path\")\n```\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Methods\n\nThese builder-pattern methods configure map behavior before opening.\n\n### WithCache: Enable Local Caching\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables a local cache that tracks all entries inserted from user space and their synchronization status.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks all entries in a local map[string]*cacheEntry\n- Records the desired action (OK, Insert, Delete) for each entry\n- Records the last error if an operation failed\n- Enables automatic error resolution (retries failed operations)\n- Returns the Map for chaining\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Tracking synchronization state\n- Automatic retry of failed operations\n- Debugging map state mismatches\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_endpoints\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithCache()\nm.OpenOrCreate()\n```\n\n### WithEvents: Enable Event Buffer\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables an event buffer that records all map operations.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `c.Enabled`: Whether to enable the buffer\n- `c.MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `c.TTL`: Time-to-live for events (0 = keep forever)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Records MapUpdate, MapDelete, and MapDeleteAll events\n- Stores events in a ring buffer (bounded size)\n- Old events are automatically removed after TTL expires\n- Uses approximately 100MB per million capacity\n- Events can be retrieved via DumpAndSubscribe()\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_connections\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 100000,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    })\nm.OpenOrCreate()\n\n// Subscribe to events\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"[%s] %s\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey())\n}, true)\n```\n\n### WithPressureMetric: Track Map Pressure\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\n\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\n\nfunc (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32)\n```\n\nEnables tracking of how full the map is (pressure as a fraction of max capacity).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calculates pressure as `(entries_in_use / max_entries)`\n- Only reports metric if pressure exceeds threshold\n- Cache must be enabled for accurate counts\n- For LRU maps, cache size may not reflect actual kernel size\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1000000, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithPressureMetric(metricsRegistry)\n\n// Metric is reported only when pressure > 0.0 (default threshold)\n\n// Or with custom threshold:\nm2 := NewMap(\"cilium_endpoints\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithPressureMetricThreshold(metricsRegistry, 0.8)  // Report only when >80% full\n```\n\n### WithGroupName: Set Metric Group\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nSets the group name used for metrics aggregation.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Maps with the same group name share metrics\n- Useful for aggregating metrics across multiple map instances\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm1 := NewMap(\"cilium_ct_tcp4\", ...).WithGroupName(\"ct\")\nm2 := NewMap(\"cilium_ct_tcp6\", ...).WithGroupName(\"ct\")\n// Both metrics reported under \"ct\" group\n```\n\n---\n\n## Query and Information Methods\n\n### Name: Get Map Name\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n```\n\nReturns the base name of the map.\n\n### Path: Get Map Path\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the full path to the pinned map on the filesystem.\n\n### FD: Get File Descriptor\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n```\n\nReturns the kernel file descriptor for the underlying eBPF map. Used for low-level operations.\n\n### Type: Get Map Type\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType\n```\n\nReturns the kernel map type (Hash, PerCPUArray, etc.).\n\n### KeySize, ValueSize, MaxEntries, Flags: Get Map Properties\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32\n```\n\nReturn the respective properties of the map.\n\n### NextKey: Get Next Key in Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error\n```\n\nGets the next key after the given key (for manual key iteration). Prefer `DumpWithCallback()` or `BatchIterator` for most cases.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling and Synchronization\n\n### Error Resolution\n\nWhen operations fail and caching is enabled, an error resolver is automatically scheduled:\n\n```go\n// If an Update() fails:\nm.Update(key, value)  // Error occurs\n// Automatically schedules error resolver...\n\n// Later, the resolver retries the operation:\nerr := m.resolveErrors(ctx)  // Runs in background\n// Tries to sync all cached entries that failed\n// Updates cache with success/failure status\n```\n\n### Cache Entry State\n\nWhen cache is enabled, each entry tracks:\n\n```go\ntype cacheEntry struct {\n    Key           MapKey\n    Value         MapValue\n    DesiredAction DesiredAction  // OK, Insert, or Delete\n    LastError     error          // Last error encountered\n}\n```\n\nThe `DesiredAction` field indicates whether an entry is in sync or has a pending operation.\n\n### Locking and Concurrency\n\n- All public methods use internal locks (RWMutex)\n- Read operations acquire read locks\n- Write operations acquire write locks\n- DumpCallback cannot call map methods (would deadlock)\n- DeleteLocked() is an exception: must be called with lock already held\n\n---\n\n## Usage Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Simple CRUD Operations\n\n```go\n// Create or open a map\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_endpoints\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &EndpointKey{},\n    &EndpointValue{},\n    10000,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed: %v\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Insert\nkey := &EndpointKey{IP: [4]byte{10, 0, 0, 1}}\nvalue := &EndpointValue{ID: 123}\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Update failed: %v\", err)\n}\n\n// Retrieve\nif v, err := m.Lookup(key); err == nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Found: %s\", v)\n}\n\n// Delete\nm.Delete(key)\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Iteration with Callbacks\n\n```go\nvar allEndpoints []*EndpointValue\n\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    ek := key.(*EndpointKey)\n    ev := value.(*EndpointValue)\n    allEndpoints = append(allEndpoints, ev)\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Dump failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Batch Iteration\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[EndpointKey, EndpointValue](m)\nctx := context.Background()\n\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    log.Printf(\"Key: %s, Value: %s\", k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Reliable Iteration with Concurrent Modifications\n\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nvar deleted []MapKey\n\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Delete failed: %v\", err)\n        } else {\n            deleted = append(deleted, key)\n        }\n    }\n}, stats)\n\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Dump failed: %v\", err)\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Deleted %d entries in %d lookups\", len(deleted), stats.Lookup)\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Event Subscription\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\n// Dump existing events and subscribe to new ones\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"[%s] %s: %v\",\n        e.GetAction(),\n        e.GetKey(),\n        e.GetLastError(),\n    )\n}, true)\n\n// Do operations...\nm.Update(key1, value1)\nm.Update(key2, value2)\nm.Delete(key1)\n\n// Events are delivered to the callback\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: Map with Caching and Error Tracking\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &ConnKey{},\n    &ConnValue{},\n    262144,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n).WithCache()  // Enable caching\n\nm.OpenOrCreate()\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Insert an entry\nkey := &ConnKey{...}\nvalue := &ConnValue{...}\nm.Update(key, value)\n\n// Cache tracks the state:\n// cache[key.String()] = {\n//   Key: key,\n//   Value: value,\n//   DesiredAction: OK (or Insert if failed),\n//   LastError: nil (or error if failed),\n// }\n\n// Error resolver runs periodically to sync failed operations\n```\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Batch Operations vs. Single Lookups\n\n- **Batch Iterator**: Efficient for iterating all/many entries\n  - Single syscall retrieves multiple entries\n  - Automatically handles buffer sizing\n  - Ideal for aggregation, monitoring, cleanup\n\n- **Single Lookup**: Better for targeted lookups\n  - Minimal overhead if you need one specific entry\n  - Direct syscall per lookup\n\n### Per-CPU Maps\n\n- Use `DumpPerCPUWithCallback()` for per-CPU maps\n- Regular dump would incorrectly retrieve only one value per entry\n- Per-CPU maps are more memory-efficient for high-frequency counters\n\n### Memory Allocation\n\n- Map creation allocates space based on `maxEntries`\n- Batch iterator automatically sizes buffers\n- Each callback receives fresh instances (safe to retain)\n\n### Locking Overhead\n\n- Read operations use read locks (concurrent)\n- Write operations use write locks (exclusive)\n- Callbacks hold locks (don't perform other operations inside callback)\n- Consider batching operations to reduce lock acquisitions\n\n---\n\n## Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Issue: DeleteAll() Not Deleting All Entries\n\n**Problem:** Entries added during iteration may survive.\n\n**Solution:** Call DeleteAll() again, or use a higher-level mechanism to prevent concurrent adds.\n\n### Issue: DumpCallback Causes Hang\n\n**Problem:** Calling map operations inside callback causes deadlock.\n\n**Solution:** Use `DeleteLocked()` specifically designed for use in callbacks, or collect items for later processing.\n\n### Issue: Map Attributes Don't Match\n\n**Problem:** Opening with different key/value size or capacity causes map deletion.\n\n**Solution:** Ensure all references use consistent map specifications, or handle recreation explicitly.\n\n### Issue: Events Not Being Captured\n\n**Problem:** Events lost between dump and subscribe.\n\n**Solution:** `DumpAndSubscribe()` handles this atomically, prevents gap.\n\n### Issue: Batch Iterator Fails with ENOSPC\n\n**Problem:** Buffer too small for a hash bucket.\n\n**Solution:** Batch iterator automatically retries with larger buffer (up to 3 times by default). Increase max retries if needed.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Key Methods\n\n| Method | Purpose | Thread-Safe | Lock |\n|--------|---------|-------------|------|\n| `Lookup()` | Get a value | Yes | Read |\n| `Update()` | Insert/update value | Yes | Write |\n| `Delete()` | Remove a value | Yes | Write |\n| `DeleteLocked()` | Remove within callback | No | (must hold write lock) |\n| `DeleteAll()` | Remove all entries | Yes | Write |\n| `DumpWithCallback()` | Iterate all entries | Yes | Read |\n| `DumpReliablyWithCallback()` | Reliable iteration | Yes | Write |\n| `IterateAll()` (BatchIterator) | Batch iteration | Yes | None (uses kernel API) |\n| `DumpAndSubscribe()` | Stream events | Yes | Read |\n| `Open()` | Load from disk | Yes | Write |\n| `OpenOrCreate()` | Open or create | Yes | Write |\n| `Close()` | Close map | Yes | Write |\n| `Unpin()` | Remove from filesystem | Yes | Read |\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
